I'm becoming a huge Luke Combs fan. I didn't want to like him at first but goddamn he's good. I've only listened to a handful of his songs, because I don't every want there to be no more new ones to listen to, but each one I've heard, I just love. The other night I thought, OK, time to try a new one. Just picked a random song off youtube. 30 seconds in and I'm crying. This one really resonated with me. I AM that hypothetical guy. The guy who didn't make it but still does it with as much heart as if he had. You've never heard of me, but I've been writing and singing for decades, I have 40 albums, all free, on my website. I know most of my "fans" personally by name. Love is really the only reason I do it. Loss does not often make me cry...but sonic beauty and the magic of the right words with the right voice and melody sure does. It can be a background vocal on a Steely Dan song or something like this. Holy shit. What a heart and what a voice!

I love this song not only because it's a great song by an artist who's work I really enjoy, but because when I first heard it, I heard my story in the music.  Not that I'm a musician, or any sort of artist.  Heck, I've never even picked up a guitar.  But like a lot of people out here working day to day in difficult jobs and doing those jobs every day not for fame, or glory, or anything special other than it's what they always did.  I've been doing the same job for 24 years now.  Sometimes, I count the days until I can make my career change (soon).  Sometimes I'll be driving home, and this song will come on, or I'll play it.  I ask myself "What would I be doing if I wasn't doing this" and the instant answer is what I'm doing now.  It fills me full of encouragement and pride for just being that guy who did his job, stuck with it even when it was terrible, and eventually figured out he found exactly what he was supposed to be doing.  On the surface, this song is about Luke, but for a lot of folks, this song is about them.  This song is about their life, their experiences, and how they feel.  And if that's not what good country music is supposed to be, then I don't know what is.
